		<date>2011-12-03</date>
		<username>sddavis63 (revsdd@gmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>Very Good Early Example Of The "Slasher" Genre</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>It would be an exaggeration to suggest that "Black Christmas" gave birth to the slasher genre. It is, however, without any doubt one of the best of the early examples of the genre, and it's very obvious that it provided at least some inspiration to what I would still consider to be the absolute best of the genre - John Carpenter's "Halloween" which came out a few years later. Carpenter (at least in his first Halloween film) learned a lesson from "Black Christmas" that a lot of later slasher films forgot - the "horror" isn't in blood and gore and overly and unnecessarily graphic violence, and you don't need naked young women to keep people watching! There are no naked young women in this (although there's sexual content in the phone calls) and "Black Christmas" actually contains surprisingly little blood and gore. Really there's only one scene - the only murder that's actually depicted, and certainly by modern standards it's not particularly graphic. The film creates its horror and suspense through the use of atmosphere and setting - and by letting the viewers in on what's happening from the start. We may not know who the killer is, but we know that the killer is in the house - which makes this all the more suspenseful, because at literally any moment of any scene set in the house, something could happen. That really very little does happen only heightens the expectation.The story revolves around a sorority house just before Christmas. As the movie opens, while a party is going on inside, a stranger (whom we never see) climbs the side of the house and gets into the attic. We're than introduced to the fact that the girls in the house have been getting a series of creepy obscene phone calls. The story builds from there as the first girl is killed, and while it takes a while for anyone else to die, that sets the stage for a truly creepy movie watching experience. The ambiguous open ending also provided obvious inspiration for later similar films that left similar open and ambiguous endings, but perhaps kept returning to the well too often.The cast is pretty decent. Apparently the producers tried to recruit some pretty big name people for this (I understand, for example, that Bette Davis was approached to play the role of the house mother) but couldn't get them. In the end, we got early film appearances from people who became fairly recognizable in later years, especially Margot Kidder, who played the drunken Barb. This is certainly deserving of recognition as an influential film that helped in the rise of a genre that has sadly now often chosen to focus on blood and gore more than story. (7/10)</fullReview>
	</review>
	<review>
		<date>2011-06-10</date>
		<username>eytand94</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Black Christmas: A Frightening Holiday Slasher</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>After "Psycho," and "Peeping Tom," people wonder whether movies like "The Texas Chainsaw Massacre" or "Halloween" invented the slew of slasher films that we get today. But hardly anyone gives credit to a 1974 film directed by Bob Clark that guarantees some serious chills. It's frightening, and weird, and yet, "Black Christmas" goes unnoticed. Perhaps the older genre fans have set aside a place in history for the film, but the more contemporary audiences hardly know it exists. This is where my review of "Black Christmas" begins.A figure approaches the Pi Kappa Sig sorority house. He climbs up the ladder to the highest window, and isolates himself in the attic. Below the attic door is a party. The sisters of the sorority (including Jess, Clare, Phyllis, and Barb) are enjoying themselves one last time before Christmas break. Many of them are leaving for the holidays while the rest stick around over the weekend to clean house with their house mother, Mrs. MacHenry(also known as Mrs. Mac). But as the obscene phone calls from an anonymous voice continue, and the girls quickly begin to disappear, the yuletide festivities are coming to a close and terror is setting in.Many movie buffs know Bob Clark for his classic comedies "A Christmas Story" and "Porky's," but don't let the fact that he directed "Black Christmas" fool you. The film is dark, and sincerely one of the scariest movies ever made.As I've stated before, the importance of the film lies within the fact that it was released four years before "Halloween." So, which film started the slasher saga? The argument has lasted forever. However, comparisons should not be drawn between the two. They are their own films with their own significance to the horror genre.The ingenious idea of inserting such a happy time of year into a time of fear and despair works extremely well. Since the film is set around Christmas time, the feeling of the holiday is evident throughout. There are decorations everywhere, as well as Christmas trees and snow. Throw the color of red onto snow, and the mood easily changes.Thanks to Roy Moore's script, not only does "Black Christmas" have a load of atmosphere, but it is also host to a series of some of the most profane, shocking, and outright creepy phone calls of all time. During the first call, the killer uses very foul language, and when Barb challenges him, his tone changes, and we hear a rather humanly voice simply say "I'm gonna kill you." From then forth, we are scared not just for ourselves, but for the sorority sisters also.You see, the characters of the film have such likability. Barb is the life of the party, but she means well. Poor Jess has a struggling relationship with her boyfriend Peter, who joyously accepts that she is pregnant but immediately becomes furious when he finds out that she's planning an abortion. These characters feel real, even when there's some comic relief from the house mother and the police department. You don't want to see them die.Telling from the phone calls, the killer keeps everything under wraps. We don't know who he is or what he plans to do, but he gives himself slight recognition of his identity by simply nicknaming himself 'Billy.' The rest of the time, we never truly see the face of the villain. In fact, we don't see much of him period. When we do feel his presence, it is in his perspective, from his point of view. While he's freaking out in the attic, we're freaking out in the attic. When he's killing somebody, we become him. It's an uncomfortable and horrifying notion, and that's why it works.In terms of acting, the cast is above average. Olivia Hussey (whose star quality was projected in "Romeo &amp; Juliet") makes for a terrific Scream Queen as Jess. Also, the early Andrea Martin and Margot Kidder keep things going as Phyllis and Barb. The appearance of genre vet John Saxon as Lieutenant Fuller is also worth noting, as well as Keir Dullea ("2001: A Space Odyssey") as Peter.All in all, it's a shame that the subordinate remake of this fright-fest got minimal attention and the original film got no attention at all. Thankfully, a DVD release has fixed the problem, and more fans have found a place in their heart for the film. It's still not as popular as "Halloween" is, but "Black Christmas" is a horror classic. It will scare and shock you, and equally provide you with a healthy dose of entertainment. This one's a must-see!P.S. The "eye behind the door" scene still keeps me up at night!</fullReview>
	</review>

		<date>2009-12-28</date>
		<username>bob_meg</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>True horror is a mood...and nothing is moodier than this</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Really good horror movies stay with you for life.Any idiot with a camera can pull you into a one-off scare with a ghoul's mask and a horrendously loud stab of music, but it takes real chops to pull off something as cumulatively horrific as Bob Clark's 1974 indie masterpiece. Watching it is like being at the center of a really macabre jigsaw puzzle that keep getting more forbidding and gruesome until you realize the last piece has your name on it.There are many exhaustive reviews (deservedly so) on this site that detail the plot, so I'm going to summarize the pieces of the puzzle that make it such a delight to return to time and again.1) The Sorority House - Just one look at this thing could send you running for the hills the way Clark, Art Director Karen Bromley, and DP Reg Morris have portrayed it. A look at the house in the daylight without the ominously warped lenses, dreary lighting, and blanketing snow reveals nothing remotely forbidding. But the thought of having to stay overnight there, as it's portrayed throughout the bulk of the film, with the majority of the occupants gone on winter break...chilling stuff. It's a character unto itself.2) Carl Zittrer's score - Quite possibly the most effective horror music soundtrack ever composed, it's a wonder for several reasons. It's economical. It uses what it needs to when it's needed. Zittrer tore up an old piano and raked the strings with a variety of odd objects, neatly echoing male lead Keir Dullea's avant garde mashing on the keys, when the character wasn't brooding ominously. Then there are the ghostly carols: "ooohs" and "aaahhhs" bent, slowed-down, sped-up, played backwards until they're ready to send you over the edge. Turn out the lights and turn up the volume on the newly remastered 5.1 soundtrack and watch your skin crawl.3) The Phone Calls - My god. Hey, there are a ton of menacing phone call movies, but nothing like this. The caller in "Black Christmas" doesn't just pant or moan or blare obscenities....he does all of this and more. "Could that possibly be ONE person?" Lynne Griffin's Claire asks the other girls early in the movie. It's a valid question, because the caller seemingly has a background soundtrack going while he's going out of his mind. Was he using a tape player? Probably, but who really cares? The point is this: the guy is obviously OUT OF HIS MIND. He's not trying to threaten, he's not trying to scare or pull a prank. He's merely letting the contents of his demented psyche loose in a torrent that's loaded with the organized chaos of a Jackson Pollack painting or John Zorn track on steroids. He laughs, screams, and sobs...many times all in the span of five seconds. The jarring vileness of these (many) calls was really toned down in the TV cut ("A Stranger In the House," which is how I first saw this --- and even hacked to pieces for late night TV it was disturbing - NBC would run it near the holidays in syndication after SNL, I remember).4. "Wrapped in Plastic" - Way before Twin Peaks, Black Christmas played with the idea of a killer "preserving" his kills with transparent casing. This is particularly morbid when they're stored in the attic of the house you happen to be occupying.5. The Totally Canadian Humor - With as much gloom and doom as BC has going for it, you'd think it would never make you crack a smile. But then again, it has two of the funniest, least self-conscious actresses playing supporting roles: Andrea Martin and Margot Kidder. And the late great Marian Waldman has the role of lifetime as a uniquely foul-mouthed, hard-drinking housemother who keeps bourbon in the toilet tank. And need I mention Doug McGrath's bumbling Sergeant Nash? His performance generates laughs and pathos simultaneously...he's a rube you can't help but pity, in a nice way.This film has an impressive fan base, and yes, it did fail when it was originally released. I hale from Peoria Illinois and it even hit our theaters a bit softly....but....the theater owners were shrewd enough to bring it back each Christmas for a limited late-night run. Why? because they knew it scared the crap out of the few who DID see it.It still does. And what better endorsement can you give a horror film?</fullReview>
	</review>

He didn't hurt them, but MAN! That gave me the same creeps that this movie did. It made me search every square inch of my house, during the day with a shotgun! I guess it just goes to show that a truly good scary movie like this one can really get under your skin! Some folks give this movie a four, three and even two star rating, which amazes me. There really is no film that compares with this one for the creepiness and dread. I think that the younger folks who are more used to the modern horror movies just can't appreciate, I believe, the genius of the suspense, dread and insane-ness of this movie.If you are twenty five and younger, try watching this movie by yourself, alone in the dark of night. 		<shortDescription>A perfect slasher if not for the bloated subplots.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>It's hard to write a review for Black Christmas. On one hand I thought much of the movie was a pathetic attempt at an emotional slasher film, and on the other hand there were scenes that were some of the best kill/scares in the history of horror movies. It's almost like Black Christmas flirts with perfection then jumps back to lame subplots. Yes, I understand that this film literally invented the slasher genre, but, no, I cannot call it perfect?I can only call certain aspects perfect.As I said, the main standout flaw is the complete lack of focus. The movie starts out in a sorority house, but from there jumps to a lot of other places to focus on characters and subplots that don't really matter to the story at all. The whole subplot of Clare's father coming to the sorority house was completely pointless by the end of the film, and just takes away from the actual story. The subplot between Jess and her boyfriend should have been cut much shorter, in order to, once again, focus on the actual story. Most of all, the subplot of the missing child still has nothing to do whatsoever with anything else in the film. I don't understand why the director takes 20 minutes to go into it, when in the end, like all the other subplots, it is nothing important. It could have easily been a passing reference instead of its own section of the film. The police scenes, also, added nothing to the story except take away from the amazing atmosphere. Everything the police scenes added could have been done with phone conversations, instead of taking up half the movie time to show things the audience could have guessed. Without all these subplots the movie would have been much, much more effective and tense.Another problem I had was the title of the film is Black Christmas, but other than the opening and one of the death scenes, nothing in this movie referenced Christmas at all. Most of the time there wasn't even snow on the ground. It would have been so much more emotionally effective if it played into the Christmas nostalgia more than it did, but the movie made the ability to play Christmas songs more of a gimmick than a plot point.Though I'm being negative with almost every aspect of the film, I really did enjoy part of it?the actual story. When the movie isn't trying to have five different subplots that go nowhere, the actual core story is done to perfection. The killer, the kills, the girls, the sorority house, the phone calls, the ending?all truly perfect, and by far the greatest slasher of all time. It's sad to see what is really a beautiful minimalist horror story turned into a bloated crime drama with more pointless subplots than kills, and that is the only thing holding this film from perfection.Overall, I wish I could go in and just watch the actual plot happen in Black Christmas, but I can't. Still, as much ranting as I did, there is something there that makes it better than so many movies that I've rated higher. Something that Hollywood forgot four decades ago. Maybe it's the fact this movie has very little blood, but is still very effective. Or, maybe, it's that the core plot was actually thought out, truly terrifying, emotionally captivating, and also something original that had never been done before it. I think that is it.4/10</fullReview>

		<fullReview>Before I sat down to watch "Black Christmas" (1975) for the first time, director Bob Clark had been two for two with me. 		<fullReview>~Spoiler~ Black Christmas is a mainstay of slasher cinema. It is one of the early films that set the standard for what would come. But if you are going to enjoy the movie, I must warn you of the hype. Black Christmas was said to have been better than Halloween by many people. I had heard this on numerous occasions before watching the film. I should have known that was untrue (Halloween in one of my favorite films). That stigma may have hindered my enjoyment of the movie somewhat. Now, don't let my complaints lead you away from the picture. Regardless of a little over hyping, it is a must-see. I wouldn't say that Halloween is in any way, shape, or form a copy of Black Christmas, but John Carpenter may owe a bit to the film. What Clark did differently was to break almost every slasher film rule before they were even written. In a normal flick, the people who have sex get it first and the heroine is always virginal. Not so in this case. The first girl killed is the virgin and our heroine is far from virginal: she's pregnant! It is very unconventional and impressive in that regard. Also impressive is John Saxon, as always. The man is a genre icon. Actually, the acting from everyone in the film is superb. I found that to be another surprising factor. But with names like Olivia Hussey, Margot Kidder, and Art Hindle I should have expected quality performances. My main complaint is the pacing and the ending. The film crawls along a bit before really picking up and the ending isn't justified. I like the fact that the killer does not die and his motives go completely unexplained. I thought that was brilliant. The problem with the ending is that there is no reason why the girl is left alone in that house. Why did everyone just disappear? Shouldn't she have been rushed to the hospital? Much like the ending of Poltergeist (where the family stays in the house one more night), there isn't sufficient enough reason for what happened. But the final shots would have lost their impact without a helpless girl still in the house. So despite a few flaws and its hype of being better than Halloween, I would say you couldn't go wrong revisiting this holiday classic. Avoid the remake AT ALL COSTS!</fullReview>

		<username>Christopher Smith</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>The movie that started it all!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Earlier this month, cult director Bob Clark tragically died in a car accident with his son. To me, Clark was a huge inspiration, an extremely talented and criminally overrated filmmaker who never got the credit he deserved. I admit to liking almost every single one of his films, although the two that will always remain my favorites are Porky's and the original Black Christmas. To truly understand the brilliance behind this masterful motion picture, one had to understand the time at which it was released. Black Christmas came out a full decade before I was born, so I'm not a person that can give a film historian perspective, but I can probably safely say that there was no other horror flick like Black Christmas upon its release in 1974, four years before John Carpenter's Halloween, which 'Christmas' influenced. Personally, I think Halloween is a slightly better movie, but this is the one that started the slasher genre, which depending on your opinion, is either a great thing or a horrible thing. Love it or hate it, there is no denying the impact.What is debatable is whether or not Black Christmas is a good movie. Some point to amateurish acting and age as factors for it not living up to its hype while others like myself argue that the only it only appears dated since all the plot devices have since been done in no less than a hundred other copycats. The acting remains a mixed bag. Olivia Hussey, Margot Kidder, and John Saxon or solid in their roles. The other sorority sisters and police don't fare so well yet none of the performances are bad enough that they ruin any of the scenes. In fact, when compared to the performances in mainstream horror released today, they are much superior. Also in contrast to today's standards, Black is Christmas is essentially gore free. Bob Clark doesn't try to gross the audience out, and the saying less is more definitely applies here.The ending is still a topic of argument among fans today. It is an ambiguous ending for sure, though I've never liked it that much. It works, but barely. Despite the ending, Black Christmas is still a favorite of mine and a must watch over the holiday season. A remake came out last year. I doubt I have to even say how it turned out. 9/10</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>rabiddog67</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Better Than Halloween</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>BLACK CHRISTMAS is one of the best of the horror genre and HALLOWEEN, although a great film itself, borrows much from this film - John Carpenter was friends with Bob Clark and even had asked Clark if he was going to do a sequel. Bob Clark, director of the excellent CHILDREN SHOULDN'T PLAY WITH DEAD THINGS and DEATHDREAM, told Carpenter that he was not going to do a sequel, but, if he was, it would be called HALLOWEEN. Carpenter's opening is very similar in style to Clark's opening, as if the killer POV camera work and the killer lurking out of the frame. Olivia Hussey is not the virginal heroine (her character is pregnant and determined to abort the baby) and a lot of film books and reviews incorrectly identify Keir Dullea as the killer when he is obviously not. I have heard complaints regarding the ending and the unknown identity of the killer because most viewers have been conditioned to have everything explained to them &amp; tied up in a neat little package, a la the ending of PSYCHO, but that only makes the film more unique. It was one of the first and the acting is superb for this type of effort. In a fair world it would be every bit as popular as HALLOWEEN, but given the amount of posts for this film, it shows that BLACK CHRISTMAS is very much appreciated by horror fans. I read an interview with Bob Clark on FANGORIA'S web site that a remake of BLACK CHRISTMAS is in the works, as well as a remake of DEATHDREAM and either a remake or sequel to CHILDREN SHOULDN'T PLAY WITH DEAD THINGS. Another great Bob Clark film worth checking out is MURDER BY DECREE, in which Sherlock Holmes takes on the Jack the Ripper slayings. It's a shame that Clark turned his back on the horror genre after BLACK CHRISTMAS and directed crap like the PORKY'S movies and LOOSE CANNONS. If he would have kept his hand at horror, I predict that he would have been one of the biggest names in the field today.</fullReview>

		<fullReview>First off, Black Christmas is not in my mind a "great horror classic", as some other people have said. Why? The girls have been receiving mysterious phonecalls from someone they call "The Moaner". The calls start out sexual in nature, but they gradually grow more macabre, with the man on the other end saying strange things in different voices. The shyest sorority girl, Claire, goes upstairs to pack, and when she goes into the closet, the killer dives out and wraps a plastic bag around her head. He then drags her into the attic, and puts her in a rocking chair. The next day, Claire's father comes to pick her up, but nobody knows where she is. It becomes a mystery as the police search for the missing Claire. Meanwhile, Mrs. Mac, the house mother, stumbles upon the killer and gets a crane hook in the face. Meanwhile, Jess admits to her boyfriend Peter that she is pregnant, but she's having an abortion. He begins to act strange, and shows off some anger problems. As Barb and Phyl are murdered by the killer, Jess gets another call. The police trace the call and realize that the calls are coming from in the house. Instead of going out, Jess goes upstairs and is attacked by the killer. She manages to escape and heads to the basement. There she runs into Peter, who she now falsely believes is the killer. He approaches her to talk, but Jess hits him over the head and kills him. The police feel the case is closed, and leave the house, leaving Jess alone to sleep off the excitement. As the credits begin to roll, we hear the phone ring once again.Now, this film has major plot spoilers, such as(warning, more spoilers): Police arrive at the home but make no effort to search it, despite two bodies having been undiscovered. (Also noteworthy is that an officer notes "The local morgue cannot handle this many bodies.") The deranged killer is able to repeat lines of dialogue from other characters on the phone, though it seems almost impossible he could have heard them despite being in the house. Despite the parent of one victim being around for the entire movie, no one suggests searching for his daughter when the mystery appears to be solved and she has not been found. Police leave the final potential victim alone in the house sleeping. (Sploliers end now)Basiclyy, this film is all blood and no story. 		<username>BaronBl00d (baronbl00d@aol.com)</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Chestnuts Roasting on an Open Fire</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This is definitely one of the best of its type; a crazed killer stalks a coed in a sorority house and unmercifully butchers her closest friends and any passersby that just happen to get in his way. What separates this from the typical slasher fare is an above-average script, above-average acting, and really good direction. Director Bob Clark, the director of such films like Children Shouldn't Play with Dead Things and Murder by Decree, seemingly does everything right in this one and makes all the right choices(well, most of the time at least). His flair for creating hauntingly eerie scenes that stay with you is first-rate. Take the first murdered girl(happens in first ten minutes). We never see the killer but just his eyes. The girl is saran-wrapped in a dress bag and set in a rocking chair with an old doll. Her presence is filmed in such a stark manner as to really set the mood of this whole film. Clark then effectively builds tension by the girl's father looking for her - as no body is found - the coed, played by the beautiful Olivia Hussey, consistently receiving phone calls from what is some sick sex pervert on the outside, the police are then brought into the mix, and finally some red herrings that throw the viewer off track a bit at the very least. All this goes on with snow, caroling, decorations, and Christmas atmosphere like one might expect in a small college town of a similar ilk. The first death scene is for my money the most effective shot and running scene in the entire film, but there are other equally brilliant shots that Clark uses to shock and create suspense. One scene in particular has Margot Kidder getting acquainted with the man with the creepy eyes with cuts(no pun intended) to children singing mellifluous carols at front door for Hussey. The acting all around is pretty good. Hussey is adequate. Kidder is too. Andrea Martin is along as well. The main policeman is John Saxon. He is pretty good and seems to flourish in roles like this in the seventies. Many films have tried to create the same effect as Black Christmas, but so few have come close at all to reaching the level of this - at least in this genre. An impressively shot film with good locations and a very effective ending.</fullReview>

		<date>2005-09-05</date>
		<username>Prolox</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Criminally underrated slasher film.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas is an effectively moody &amp; very scary horror thriller, that will shred the nails of even the most jaded of horror fans! Sadly it also carries the reputation of being one of the most criminally underrated &amp; forgotten of the slasher films amongst todays horror fans &amp; critics. True the film wasn't as successful box office wise as HALLOWEEN &amp; Friday the 13th, nevertheless I think it's perfectly fair to say that Black Christmas created the rules of the genre, Friday the 13th &amp; HALLOWEEN merely just took those &amp; ran with them &amp; just happened to have more success than this one did. The film is unbearably suspenseful at times as director (the late) BOB CLARK infuses the film with several chilling moments that could rival any moments of suspense &amp; terror of some of the most reviled horror films that fans hold dear. Make no mistake about it, the minute it starts, Black Christmas wastes no time in delivering the chills one expects from a truly great scary, moody &amp; suspenseful horror film, as we see the killer (who remains unseen throughout the whole movie, with the exceptions of his hand, eyes &amp; shadow) stalking around the sorority house, in an opening scene John Carpenter swiped for the opening of his horror classic HALLOWEEN four years later, as we see things through the killer's point of view. The final twenty minutes of the film are a real nail shredder, as the heroine quickly learns that not only is she the last one left alive in the house, but also the very maniac she fears, is waiting for her upstairs! Despite it's low budget, the acting here blows practically every other bit of acting in a horror film out of the water! The cast chosen here are really talented &amp; help make their fun characters all the more interesting, particularly MARGOT KIDDER as as an alcoholic, bad girl sorority sister &amp; OLIVIA HUSSEY as the lead heroine. Director BOB CLARK shows what a talent he is &amp; delivers some of the best, if not the best directing in a horror film, in fact Clark himself is perhaps the most criminally underrated film-maker to ever step foot in the film industry &amp; I say that because he created two film genres, that has led to financial success at the box office for Hollywood, one is the "slasher film" but also the "teen sex comedy" that he helped usher in a few years after this film with PORKY'S. Both PORKY'S &amp; Black Christmas helped shape up both genres that are pretty prevalent in the film industry today &amp; sadly Clark doesn't get credited with creating either. Another sad thing about Black Christmas being an underrated gem in the horror genre, is the fact that the films main villain (BILLY) is hardly (if ever) listed as one of the most terrifying villains in horror filmdom &amp; I say that's sad, because he should get the same recognition as guys like Jason Freddy &amp; Michael &amp; Leatherface, since he is equally as scary as either one of these popular horror icons. By the films ending, we never really know why Billy has selected the sorority house as the site of his murdering spree, who he is, why he does what he does etc. &amp; while this usually works against most horror films &amp; horror movie villains &amp; can make them less interesting, the truth is it works in Black Christmas favour, by the films end credits, perhaps the most terrifying thing about him, is simply the fact Billy has not been captured, in fact he's still on the loose &amp; lurking around the attic of the sorority house which the camera pans up to after visiting the scenes of his crimes (Another thing Carpenter swiped for HALLOWEEN, by having that films villain the crazed Michael Myers also still be alive &amp; on the loose &amp; visiting the scenes of his crimes by the time that films credits have run). While mentioning Carpenter's classic, I also have to make mention that minus the things I already mentioned, another thing that connects the two, is that both films villains are very similar, not in terms of personality (Michael is silent, this guy talks, though anything he says is down right chilling) but in the simple fact that it could be argued that both villains are lightly hinted at as being demoniacally possessed. What with Michael's habits of appearing &amp; re-appearing in certain places like a ghost, him surviving six gun shot wounds, various stabbings &amp; a fall off a building &amp; this killer, who's phone calls sounds like several voices talking a once, with some of the voices sounding very inhuman. Even though we hardly see him in the movie, we can still feel this killers presence around, even in scenes he's not in, where people are just talking &amp; that in my eyes is a true testament to how scary Black Christmas actually is. There is no gore on hand, as practically all the kills are done off screen, but they are very inventive, particularly the opening kill of the one sorority sister, who is smothered to death with a plastic bag over her face &amp; then placed in a rocking chair in the attic to look out the attic window (which could arguably be construed as a back handed tribute to PSYCHO (1960) in a kill that was such a favourite of those who saw it, that it now adorns practically every video box art &amp; is one of the best images the film is known for. Remade in 2006**** stars</fullReview>
	</review>

Jess and Lt Fuller are coming to the same conclusions. Lt Fuller follows this lead to a destroyed piano in the conservatory and Jess's greatest fears are allayed by Phyllis who reminds her that Peter was visiting them when the phone stalker dialed them up making him the suspect impossible.This films suffers a lot of errors in continuity and gaping plot holes. If the phone lines are only in living room, the hall, and Mrs Mac's room how is the killer moving around undetected? There isn't a phone jack in the attic. And how come the girl's failed to hear him yelling from Mrs Mac's room? And how did he leave the house, kill patrolman Jennings, and get back inside the house undetected by the sorority sisters nor the search party outside? Yeah, he could of went back down the lattice from the attic window and again back up? Still... I ain't buying it. Unless our killer is a flipping ninja yeah that is what he is. *Gives self-induced facepalm* D'oh.This is a classic slasher maybe deserves a better rating but I didn't find it all that scary, but rather silly, I didn't appreciate how forcibly determined the film chose to misdirect me. Actually, it would have been an improvement to this film if Peter did indeed suffer a mental breakdown leading to a homicidal psychosis. Keir Dullea fit the role like a hand-in-glove.</fullReview>

		<date>2010-12-19</date>
		<username>Scarecrow-88</username>
		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Black Christmas</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>A real troubled psychopath has found a new home in the attic of a sorority and he often calls them to rant and rave perversities and memories which haunt him from the past involving Billy and Agnes. Who these two are isn't as important as the fact that the person blabbering incoherently and loudly about them is extremely dangerous and unhinged. While some of the sorority girls go on their Christmas vacations, a few remain and they are sharing their college house, unbeknownest to them, with the nutcase who continues to telephone harass them. When one of the girls is suffocated with a plastic bag, her body sitting comfortably in a rocking chair by the killer in the attic, the victim's father will come looking for her. His search, along with the scary phone calls, might just get the police into action..that and another missing girl in the area who was supposed to be coming home by way of the nearby park. What I think allows BLACK Christmas to persevere is the balance of laughs and chills. The mere thought of your house being invaded, without your knowledge, by a real wacko is frightening enough, not to mention the fact that he torments you by phone over and over with horrifying ramblings which make little sense, for the exception that the tone is disturbing. To open the film with the killer climbing up the wall and into the attic through a point-of-view shot really sets the viewer on edge for we experience his invasion personally..in his body, through his sight, we enter the house and know he, in essence, now has an advantage over those within the building. Clark uses the Keir Dullea character of Peter as a red herring, but I never felt he was the one behind the murders in BLACK Christmas. What is established though, and effectively I believe, is Peter's questionable sanity. Peter is quite an intense individual who can act irrational and immature. His whole piano recital goes haywire because Peter reacts through the musical arrangement the anger he feels towards pregnant girlfriend, Jess(Olivia Hussey), who wants an abortion. So even if he isn't the killer, Peter is certainly a bit suspect in behavior. Margot Kidder is obviously the comic relief, although I found her a bit sad because it seems she's using liquor and acidic humor as a means to hide certain underlying troubles and disappointments in life. Her fellatio scene with hapless Sargeant Nash(Doug McGrath) is recognized as a highlight, but her outbursts towards some of the girls(and their reactions of dismay)proves she can be a polarizing presence to those around her. John Saxon is Lt. Fuller, the detective who goes out of his way to find the missing girl(s)in his sleepy Canadian college town. Marian Waldman as the profane, alcohol-guzzling housemother, Mrs. Mac, also earns some giggles as she turns up various liquor bottles she has hidden in the house while grumbling about the demands of her position. James Edmond as the worried father, Mr. Harrison, dedicated to finding his daughter and Art Hindle, in an early part, as the girl's concerned boyfriend. Hussey, the lovely and elegant heroine who loses all of her friends while almost exclusively on the premises(memorable scene being when one of them is stabbed repeatedly with a glass unicorn while her Jess listens intently to carolers), is the anchor of the film, responsible for having to endure those burdensome phone terrorisms. Andrea Martin, the other sorority sister, Phyl, who is one of the unfortunates who stays at the house during the Christmas holiday. Certainly a loaded cast full of talent, but it's really the subject matter and Clark's ingenious methods of mystery in regards to the menace that really lifts this masterpiece of dread to its cult status which maintains thirty years later.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>Unsettling, but...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Being a horror film afficiando, I headed off to one of my local videostores to catch up on horror films that I ought to have seen for one reason or another. One of the films I picked up was this one, having read that it was probably the first slasher flick, which qualified it to my list. After watching it, I thought that it was very unsettling, but was it REALLY scary? And was it any good? Well, sort of. The problem with the film is that one, I couldn't care less about the characters, and when they go about acting like total idiots I even caught myself mumbling: "if he/she/it gets killed now he/she/it's got him/her/itself to blame". This keeps the film from really being scary, plus that, and this probably wasn't the case for the audience when it was released, the ending is so unbelievably predictable that it's plain silly.WARNING! SPOILER!I mean, if you have a long cameraroll that drifts from he bed where the heroine lies across the hall, doesn't that give it all away? And they basically signal that it's coming, I mean, why else would everybody leave the room? I called it right when the scene started!END OF SPOILERNow, don't get me wrong, it is a pretty good film. Now it's time to compare it to the other film of this kind, John Carpenter's "Halloween". There are similarities, but there is one significant difference. In "Halloween", we know who the killer is a couple of minutes in, in "Black Christmas" we don't. And that makes a bigger difference than one might think. One film which is a big ripoff of "Black Christmas" though is "Friday the 13th", which is built up in a similiar fashion, but is indeed a MUCH MUCH worse film. But back to "Black Christmas" vs "Halloween", the question now is, which one do I prefer? The answer is easy, I'll pick "Halloween" any day of the week. Why? Easy, Carpenter is a much more skilled director than Bob Clark and it shows in a major way. Clark manages to build an effective mood, but the mood Carpenter builds is more menacing than Clark could build in his dreams. SPOILER!Second of all, in "Halloween", the characters act more human. When they are given a chance to escape they take it, they don't go out to investigate.END OF SPOILERNext is the camerawork. It is similiar, but it's far more slick in "Halloween". The same goes for just about everything else in the film. But back to just "Black Christmas", the film is definitely worth the price of rental, since it is after all a sort-of classic. I personally don't think it's good enough to be classic in terms of quality, but does belong on the cult classic list since it helped spawn the genre that "Psycho" laid the building blocks for. But it's definitely not a masterpiece. According to me, anyway.</fullReview>

This was a slasher movie that pre-dated Halloween and Friday the 13th... it probably didn't seem as cliched then as it does now. In fact, a lot of scary movies that came out later sure seem to have been influenced by this one. Young women in a large, spooky sorority house are plagued by weird, obscene phone calls... and then mysteriously they start to vanish, one by one... victims of a crazed psycho killer (sound familiar yet?) The movie is competently-made... but the acting is very uneven. SCTV's Andrea Martin plays one of the sorority girls and it's a little difficult to accept her in a "straight" role... as accustomed as we are to see her making fun of movies like this. Margot Kidder plays another of the girls... the wild, outspoken, rebellious one (might as well have a target pinned to her back... dang!) The rest of the actors are Canadian performers of varying degrees of competence. Some of the scenes are suspenseful... even if some of the goings-on defy logic and/or common sense. 		<username>piratecannon</username>
		<score>0.6</score>
		<shortDescription>Psycho Stalks Sisters</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Director Bob Clark is best known for his 1983 film A Christmas Story, the feel-good tale of a child who wants a Red Rider BB gun from Santa Claus. What a lot of people don't know, however, is that Mr. Clark has approached the holiday season from a much darker perspective. And his 1974 slasher, Black Christmas, is surprisingly effective.I'll be completely honest. I expected shoddy acting and lame scares to abound. Black Christmas does have its fair share of the preceding, but it also generates a somber, brooding atmosphere that's heightened by the frenzied piano stylings of a college student, named Peter, who appears to be on the verge of mental collapse. This guy is dating one of the sisters who lives in the sorority house where the bulk of the terror takes place?this comes in the form of harassing phone calls and some odd, funhouse-mirror-style first-person perspectives?and he's meant to be suspect number one. The elusive psycho's identity is never revealed, and it's clear that screenwriter Roy Moore wants us to believe that Peter is, in fact, the bad guy, but some last-second revelations result in the old switcheroo. This, along with a number of other strategies used in Black Christmas, seem frighteningly clichéd in this day and age, but I can only imagine that they were fairly groundbreaking during their own time (okay, so Psycho is really the movie that spawned the modern slasher, but let's at least give credit to a movie that's notably more tense than most of the horror to emerge from contemporary Hollywood).As previously disclosed, this isn't to say that Black Christmas doesn't have faults. Some of the acting?and corresponding character responses? to what's going on in and around said sorority house are completely unbelievable. The father of a missing sister, for example, calmly explores the campus when his daughter doesn't show-up for a rendezvous they had planned early one afternoon. Even after the police get involved and it's somewhat clear that foul play is afoot, this guy never exhibits any urgent sense of emotion to locate his daughter. There's also the presence of a pointless old woman who, for one inexplicable reason or another, lives in the sorority house. She curses and has liquor stashed in books and septic tanks throughout the home. I'm guessing she was meant to serve as some sort of comic foil, but she's more of an annoyance than anything else.That's Black Christmas in a nutshell. Would I recommend it as a cozy little holiday horror movie? Sure. It's certainly not bad, and it has its creepy moments, but don't expect the reinvention (or invention?) of the wheel.</fullReview>

		<score>1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A terrifying masterpiece of the macabre!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>It's Christmas break at a sorority house, the girls (Margot Kidder, Olivia Hussey and Andrea Martin) are planning things for Christmas vacation. Until a mysterious stranger makes weird phone calls as he torments the girls then sneaks into the attic of the house as he starts to kill some of the girls one by one. The police are concerned by strange murders going on especially the discovery of a dead 13 year old girl in a park but can the cops find this psychopath or will he have his bloody hands on the entire household? Suspenseful and masterful psychological horror slasher flick from Canada and writer-director Bob Clark who would later give us "Porky's" and "A Christmas Story". It's a true masterpiece of the slasher genre in the 70's with "Texas Chainsaw Massacre", "Halloween", "Torso" and Mario Bay's "Twitch of The Death Nerve" (a.k.a. Bay of Blood) but this was before "Halloween" hit the screen 4 years later. The film also stars John Saxon who is one of cult cinema's best actors, it's a scary and chilling skin-crawler that will keep you guessing till the very end. Unlike most slasher movies which uses gore, this one uses characterizations and tension rather then just brainless blood-buckets. This is a true underrated horror masterpiece that every horror fan should seek and paved the way for other slasher flicks like "Halloween", "A Nightmare on Elm Street", "Friday The 13th", "Maniac", "Sleepaway Camp", "The Burning", "Scream" etc. as it ranks up with "Psycho".</fullReview>

		<username>fertilecelluloid</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>Still a good movie, but not a horror classic</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I enjoyed my first viewing of Bob Clark's "Black Christmas" more than my most recent viewing. I still feel that the film is an accomplished piece of work and established a structure and screen language that have been much imitated. The characters are intelligent and screenwriter Roy Moore even takes a shot at the abortion issue.The obscene phone calls made by the killer are truly obscene (much use of the word "c**t"), and his psychotic rants are rather amusing, if not a little disturbing. The killer's POV, which opens the movie, is effective, and the image of a suffocated victim lurking by a window is a memorable one.The film doesn't scare me, though, or make me uneasy. Perhaps I've seen too many horror films. I can't fault Clark for his direction or Carl Zitter for his atmospheric score, more a soundscape than a traditionally structured series of compositions. I simply found the film a bit slow the last time around.Clark's "Deathdream" is one of my favorite horror films of all time (see my review), and it was made before "Christmas". Certainly, "Christmas" is a larger scale production, but, for me, it does not possess the intimacy of "Deathdream" and the sense of crawling horror. It plays more like a mystery than a horror film and lacks the tragedy that made "Deathdream" so effective. Bob Clark may have thought so, too, because "Christmas"'s score sounds exactly like "Deathdream" (same composer), there is a creepy rocking chair (like the one "Andy" used in Deathdream"), and the house exteriors look like the house exteriors in, yes, you guessed it, "Deathdream".Still, a very good movie, but not, for me, a horror classic.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<fullReview>It's not a movie with a great or original story (which horror movie does anyway?) or approach but this is simply one fine and effective genre movie, with a fine premise, good settings and some wonderful genre moments.Amazing thing is that director Bob Clark started his career with movies like this but soon continued on making movies such as "Porky's" and "Baby Geniuses", which is obviously a totally different genre. A waste of his talent? Well, in all honesty horror movies from the '70's are definitely better ones than the ones from the '80's of '90's, so I'm not too sure about it actually if Clark would had continued to direct horror movies during his later career those movies would had been as good as this one, mostly in terms of style.'70's movies of course have a very distinctive style and atmosphere. Some of the best and most classic horror movies also date back from the '70's. Movies such as "The Exorcist", "The Omen", "Don't Look Now", "Halloween" oh and I can just go on and on. This movie wasn't the first slasher and it also wasn't the most influential or best known one (credit for that still mostly goes to John Carpenter's "Halloween") but it's nevertheless obvious that this movie inspired later film-makers and is a fine example of the genre from the '70's.It's a really effective horror movie, that features all of the right required ingredients. It doesn't make this the most original genre movie with its style or approach but it's simply one fine executed one. The movie has a good dark and mysterious atmosphere and it also really knows to be scary in parts. Especially the phone calls within the movie, which play a key part, are really scary. I don't know what it is but phone calls are always scary and effective material for horror movies. Just think about movies such as "Scream", "When a Stranger Calls" or "Sorry, Wrong Number".What also helps the movie is its atmospheric musical score from Carl Zittrer, who used to work a lot with Bob Clark during his career.The movie also really has a great cast with actors you wouldn't necessarily normally expect in a genre movie such as this one. Margot Kidder is really great in this movie, in a fairly early role from her. The movie also stars Keir Dullea, who unfortunately doesn't ever star in that many movies.A great movie for the fans of the genre, as well as to everyone else for all that matter.8/10http://bobafett1138.blogspot.com/</fullReview>

		<username>slayrrr666 (slayrrr666@yahoo.com)</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A tad overrated, but still a great movie</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>"Black Christmas" is a pretty disappointing proto-slasher.**SPOILERS**Gathering for a Christmas party, Jess Bradford, (Olivia Hussey) Barbara Coard, (Margot Kidder) Phyllis Carlson, (Andrea Martin) and Claire Harrison, (Lynne Griffin) along with Mrs. MacHenry, (Marian Waldman) all prepare for their Sorority party. As the night goes on, they are continued to be inundated with a series of obscene phone calls that many say have been going on for awhile. As they take place, they also find that some of the other sorority members have gone missing, and pleading with Lieutenant Kenneth Fuller, (John Saxon) does nothing as he claims to be more prioritized with another case. Forced back in the sorority house as there's nothing the police can do, the calls continue and the others disappear, making the others realize that there's something wrong with the calls. Checking back in with the police, they realize that there's a killer in the house and try to get out before they encounter him.The Good News: There wasn't a whole lot to this one, as it was surprisingly disappointing. The main source this one gets right is the mystery of the killer. We never see the killer's face aside from a hand and a spastic looking eyeball. We never learn the killer's true motives or identity, or why he decided to plague this particular sorority house. That is just eerie and really makes the killer a lot more fearsome when the identity remains a secret. The film does a spectacular job of making the killer feel really threatening without doing a whole lot. Even more important is that, early in the film, the killer establishes a trademark method of operation, which is maintained rather faithfully throughout the movie. Immediately after dispatching a victim, he immediately places an obscene phone call to the house. That works wonders, especially when it's revealed that this has been going on prior to the beginning of the film. During the first phone call, one remarks that it's the moaner again the, meaning that he has called before. This fits with the later fact that several townspeople have been raped on the college campus during the recent weeks. There's also the fact that the killer starts toying with them in incredibly perverse ways and the tormenting gets more and more vulgar as time goes on. That allows for more fear from the killer, and all of the calls actually go a long way; as well as the other tactics, to make the killer something to be feared. When it switches over to the later calls, it gets even more disturbing and even more furious. From this point on, the caller exhibits obvious symptoms of multiple-personality-disorder, and we hear him switching between three different voices within the course of one call, often times the different voices even overlap one another. It's a neat trick, and again goes even further towards making the killer the ultimate creep. From the moments where just the POV is seen running across the landscape with just the breathing voice heard to the sense of humor displayed with the strangulation gag that comes from the simply mind-blowing original finale, the killer here is one of the best in the genre. A couple of the attacks are pretty cool as well, especially the bedroom one where the screams are drowned out by the caroling group downstairs as well as one where a victim is lured in and attacked with a giant pulley system. These here provide the film's only good points.The Bad News: This one here wasn't all that impressive, with it's laurels really resting on a couple of areas. This one has such a dull and boring middle section that most of the problems are found here. The film decides to stack in as many different scenes and subplots in here to stretch the film out that after a while it gets incredibly dull and boring. From the pregnancy subplot that has nothing to do at all with any of the film's proceedings once it's given to the missing towns-person going missing along with the search by the police, this film is super padded out to ridiculous lengths. These take up a large amount of the film's time to take in with certain areas of the plots that contain nothing of importance in the final count. There's also the fact that this one is a complete mystery surrounding the killer. While it's nice to finally get a mystery, not even being sure of the killer's name is taking it a bit too far. This occurs in a conversation as a line that the person on the other end spouts, yet nothing is confirmed as to whether it's the actual name or whether it's a person who caused the psycho to go homicidal. Other names are dropped in the course of the conversations, but again, not even having something as simplistic as a name is a big shame in the film. Other factors in here, from the reasoning behind the rampage to the motive of selecting this particular sorority, manage to force into the viewer such a state of confusion that there's a really volley of emotions over being scared and annoyed over the killer. The fact that a lot of questionable tactics are put into play over what he tries to do with them or not is another big factor with this one, and in the end, this one ends up feeling very disappointing.The Final Verdict: With a lot of dull moments in this one and a couple of somewhat decent moments, this one comes across as a merely disappointing effort. This is one really for those who have a big fascination with the early-going slashers or are into the film's positives, while those who prefer faster-paced fare should seek caution.Rated R: Graphic Language and Graphic Violence</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>A little dated, but still better than 60% of horror films released lately.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Every time a remake is released (which is almost every week) these days I feel more compelled to seek out the source material to see why it needed remaking in the first place, as in 90% of cases the remake is worse or just as lousy as the original.I never saw the remake of Black Christmas, it looked altogether too teen-y for me and I'm not a big slasher flick fan anyway. But I did read something that said that it was a remake of perhaps the first slasher flick, which at least piqued my interest as it is always interesting to see where certain genres originated.After viewing what is immediately evident is that 35 odd years ago it was apparently unsettling enough to simply set up the kill and then have the killer do the rest. There are no intricate 7 minute "creeping through the halls" or red herring scares here, the victims decide to do something, enter the room in which they will do that thing, and the killer does the rest quickly and in straightforward fashion.Nowadays to achieve the same result the filmmakers have to build the tension or ramp up the gore, guess which one they normally go for ('eh Eli?).The supposed big twist (copied by Scream) is actually made evident in the very opening scene, as we are introduced to "Stalker-Cam" (TM) as someone cases a house from the outside, while a party seems to be going on inside. Said individual then climbs up and into the attic of the house.It turns out we are in what I think they call a frat-house in the US, a communal dorm for students, in this case all female with a middle aged, seemingly alcoholic dorm mother.The girls are having an end of term party before either heading home or settling in for the Christmas holidays. The party is interrupted by an obscene phone call, as the girls are all in their late teens / early 20s they put the phone on speaker and have a chuckle. Of course some are offended and others get into the swing of things and actually try to talk back to the caller, but ultimately no harm is done and they hang up, thinking that's that.Seeing as the film doesn't waste time in building tension or suspense, we get a fair bit of time spent getting to know the individual girls, there are no cardboard cut-outs here (I'm talking to you Friday the 13th remake!), there are drunken sluts, naive young women and other normal girls, same as every group of students. They are beset by the usual circumstances that occur to the age group, horny suitors, teenage pregnancy, busybody adults and the allure of alcohol and mischief.When quite suddenly (to them at least) a member of their number goes missing, they don't just shrug it off as so many crappy horror movies do today by saying "Oh, she must have gone to the shops" or "She'll show up", they treat the disappearance seriously, and as they care for their missing friend so too does the audience care more.The crank calls keep coming and they keep getting more and more disturbing, I would question why the girls keep listening but it is a movie after all. In between a small collection of bodies builds up, again this isn't a 73 dead slash fest as many are today and the remaining girls come across all sorts of roadblocks when trying to solve the issue, not the least of which is incompetent police work.When the ending comes it is in keeping with the rest of the flick, straightforward and basic, and there is no realllll surprise unless you have never ever seen a horror film in your life. What would concern though is the outrageously terrible police investigation that follows that wraps everything up so nicely whilst ignoring so many events and incidents.Again, this was the 70s, maybe they just didn't care too much back then about the details.Final Rating ? 7 / 10. You aren't going to see anything new, but I'd rather watch this than most big budget horror remakes churned out these days.If you liked this review (or even if you didn't) check out oneguyrambling.com</fullReview>

		<date>2007-02-11</date>
		<username>BA_Harrison</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>It's good, but it's no 'Halloween'.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Canadian director Bob Clark's Black Christmas (1974) gets a lot of love these days from many horror fans who cite it as the inspiration for John Carpenter's classic, Halloween, and some even claim it to be the original slasher film?the one that started the sub-genre that spawned not just Michael Myers but countless other masked maniacs. Whilst I am not in total agreement with them (Mario Bava's Bay Of Blood, for example, follows the body count style of the genre and was made in 1971), I do agree that this film must have been highly influential on Mr.Carpenter, who obviously modelled some of his film's scenes on Black Christmas's best moments (although Halloween is still the superior movie, in my humble opinion).Clark sets his seminal shocker in a sorority house during the Christmas holidays, where a group of young women are killed one by one by a crazy, ranting maniac who has also been scaring them with a series of sick telephone calls. Starring Keir Dullea, Olivia Hussey, Margot Kidder and cult movie favourite John Saxon, the film has no shortage of talent in the acting department, and Clark delivers quite a few stylish directorial flourishes that really help to crank up the tension.From the get go, Black Christmas introduces plot elements and visual techniques that were to become a staple of stalk 'n' slash movies for years to come: creepy POV shots; the careful framing of shots to reveal movement in the background; the killer's heavy breathing on the soundtrack; the final victim frantically fleeing from the maniac (after having discovered the mutilated bodies of her friends). We also get to see where When A Stranger Calls (1979) got its 'We've traced the call... it's coming from inside the house' moment from?the exact same thing occurs in Black Christmas!Also particularly effective are the telephone calls made by the maniac; a mixture of unintelligible ranting, guttural moans, violent threats and crude obscenities, they are very unsettling and help convey exactly how demented the (unseen) murderer truly is. Another factor that adds to the creepy vibe of the film is the fact that we never get to find out who the killer is or why he is attacking these seemingly innocent girls. Even at the end, Clark gives nothing away about his identity. By not giving us any background details, or any motivation for his actions, he turns the killer into a 'bogeyman' (another idea borrowed by Carpenter for his movie).Unfortunately, there are also several things that let the film down slightly.Firstly, there is a lack of any really likable characters: Hussey's heroine is rather selfish, Kidder's character is a loud mouthed drunk, and Dullea plays a rather dull and obsessive pianist. Worst of all is the drunken house mother, a nasty woman who thankfully meets a suitably violent end. At least Carpenter had the good sense to make some of his victims a little more likable, thus actually making the audience give a damn about whether they lived or not.Clark also neglects to put in any real scares; creepiness the film has in spades, but genuine shocks are in short supply. And with the few deaths being rather bloodless, the 'yuck' factor is also kept fairly low (unless you find endless shots of a body with a plastic bag over its head particularly nauseating).Lastly, Clark tries to inject some humour into the proceedings, but fails spectacularly: Kidder's weak prank about fellatio is desperately unfunny and the drunken house mother's search for booze is truly cringe-worthy.Black Christmas is a film that all horror fans should see, since it helped to define a whole horror sub-genre, but to say it is better than Halloween is definitely going a step too far.</fullReview>
	</review>

	<review>
		<date>2004-10-16</date>
		<username>MARIO GAUCI (marrod@melita.com)</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>BLACK Christmas (1974)</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I had read quite a few reviews of BLACK Christmas (1974) before purchasing it, never having watched the film before. I certainly felt elated afterwards that it was very much worth picking up. I am saying this because, having grown up on Alan Frank's book HORROR MOVIES - in which this was not mentioned at all! - I didn't quite know what to expect. It's certainly one of the finest 'slasher' films I have ever watched, not that I can say I'm a rabid fan of this sub-genre.As with most of the landmark horror films of the 1970s, BLACK Christmas was a low-budget production but the film is very well-made and this factor never becomes a problem. The screenplay by Roy Moore was fairly original for its time, though it's since been copied ad nauseam: the mostly young cast does extremely well here - it helps that many were professional actors, making the audience care for the characters' fate - which cannot be said for virtually any of its contemporaries (not even John Carpenter's HALLOWEEN [1978]). Again, it skilfully integrates generous doses of humor to offset the generally high-strung and claustrophobic mood. Tension is admirably built-up and sustained throughout, particularly during the last half-hour. The murder scenes, though not too many in number, are certainly very effective - and thankfully done without the need for extensive use of gore.Technically, the film is also well up to par: Reg Morris' cinematography superbly captures the sinister atmosphere of the house making it a major character in the proceedings, as well as the killer's state of mind through a frequent use of the subjective camera. Expert editing keeps the audience on edge throughout, but it is at its most effective during Margot Kidder's death scene (a veritable Argento moment) and the finale. Carl Zittrer's unusual and largely dissonant score is very unsettling, and another big plus. The killer's attitude reminded me a bit of Andy Robinson's psycho in DIRTY HARRY (1971), and the weird and pretty haunting sounds he makes (the girls themselves dub him 'The Moaner') were probably inspired by Mercedes McCambridge's demon voice in THE EXORCIST (1973) - but they are even more impressive, and scary, for not showing the person making them!The comedy element of this film is worth a special mention: from the posters hung up on the walls of the sorority to Marian Waldman's boozy antics as the contemptuous house mother to Margot Kidder's turtle anecdote during a party and her 'telephone exchange' scene at the Police Station (which, later on, is also beset by a trigger-happy old man who literally shoots one of the officers in the ass!), the film is quite hilarious at times - which, in a film of its type, is not easy to come across and even harder to pull off! Still, BLACK Christmas' most memorable comic foil is Douglas McGrath playing a baffled cop put upon by just about everyone, including his own colleagues and superiors; these scenes are far better handled than the sorry attempts at comedy in Wes Craven's THE LAST HOUSE ON THE LEFT (1972), that's for sure!The leading roles are nicely filled: Olivia Hussey projects more than just beauty as the strong-willed heroine; Keir Dullea essays his relatively difficult role admirably; Margot Kidder is impressive in what she has to do, and probably influenced her later casting as Lois Lane in SUPERMAN - THE MOVIE (1978); John Saxon is suitably commanding as the Police Lieutenant intent on capturing the madman. If there is one thing about the film which I find unsatisfying is the lack of sufficient clarity in the killer's backstory (reminding me of Dario Argento's OPERA [1987] which I have only watched for the first time a couple of weeks ago). I know this was probably done on purpose but, usually in this type of film, all the plot threads are neatly woven by the end - whereas here we rather emerge from the whole enthralling ordeal (echoed, to a certain extent, by HALLOWEEN's conclusion) none the wiser!Much has been said of the film's Original Aspect Ratio. The end titles clearly give this as being shot in Panavision, so I don't know why anyone would prefer to watch it 'full frame'. Actually, once I had watched it I couldn't envision the film in this way, and sure enough the scenes that appear in the documentary are not as effective for this very reason! The DVD supplements are extensive but, all in all, something of a mixed bag: the two Audio Commentaries are very interesting, even though quite a bit of info is repeated verbatim elsewhere on the disc - also, Bob Clark's track (which is fuller than the John Saxon/Keir Dullea one) quite often suffers from poor audio making his comments hard to understand; the three interview segments, two of them with Saxon and another one with Clark, deal with the rest of their work as well as their obvious fondness for BLACK Christmas; though it basically covers all grounds, the documentary disappoints slightly due to the amateurishness of its production (it certainly pales in comparison with Blue Underground's or Laurent Bouzereau's efforts which grace numerous DVD editions of classic films) - still, my favorite bit is the greatly moving anecdote involving Edmond O'Brien's failing health which prevented him from taking the role later filled by John Saxon; numerous trailers and radio spots (narrated by a familiar voice later to play a prominent part in Clark's MURDER BY DECREE [1978]) are great fun, as is the photo gallery which features a good selection of stills, posters and behind-the-scenes shots; finally, the alternate credit sequences and reversible cover art are nice to have, too.The disc also includes a special preview of MURDER BY DECREE by way of its theatrical trailer (which, apparently, is in pretty bad shape!), announcing it to be coming soon on Critical Mass DVD. Does anyone have any idea when this will be released and what supplements will be included - the film is certainly intriguing and Anchor Bay's DVD (that was only released in January) seems to be quite satisfactory, but who knows if it could be improved?Having watched BLACK Christmas, I'm certainly interested in catching up with other Bob Clark horror films, particularly his two earlier efforts - CHILDREN SHOULDN'T PLAY WITH DEAD THINGS (1972; coming soon on R2 DVD from Anchor Bay UK) and DEATHDREAM (1972; aka: DEAD OF NIGHT).</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>Paul Andrews (poolandrews@hotmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Horrendously overrated as far as I'm concerned.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas is set in a girls sorority house around Christmas, one of the girls Clare Harrison (Lynne Griffin) is spending the festive season with her father at home but is brutally killed in her room before she meets up with him. The next morning &amp; her dad (James Edmond) raises the alarm &amp; contacts the police who organise a search where they find the dead body of a young child, meanwhile the sorority house has been receiving obscene phone calls which they tell the police about. Lieutenant Fuller (John Saxon) decides all the clues point the the sorority house with very good reason as there's a killer on the loose inside...This Canadian production was produced &amp; directed by Bob Clark &amp; I have to say I think Black Christmas is vastly overrated, considered by some to be the very first slasher film ever made I'd personally say it's more of a thriller although I can see why some would say that. The script by Ray Moore is very serious &amp; tries to build tension up &amp; remain quite taught but I have to say I was pretty bored by it. It takes ages to do anything &amp; then we get the god awful ending, some people complain about horror films not having much of a story &amp; Black Christmas would almost certainly give those people more ammunition as the killer is never seen, the killer's motives are never revealed neither is the basic question of who he is. I'm sorry but even Jason Voorhees &amp; Freddy Kruger had back stories, at least they had some sort of motive no matter how flimsy it was while here in Black Christmas there is nothing. Some may like the ambiguity &amp; sure it works well enough for most of the film but I'd have liked some sort of pay-off, some sort of explanation, some sort of twist, some sort of story behind the killer &amp; a proper ending, you see Black Christmas doesn't so much as end as just stops. On the plus the plus side it's watchable, the character's are good &amp; more human than in a lot of horror films although for me that's just not enough to want to sit through 100 minutes of this again.Since it was Chritsmas Day only a few days ago Black Christmas was an appropriate film to sit down &amp; watch last night &amp; director Clark does a really good job here &amp; the films best asset is it's atmosphere &amp; style, there are some great point-of-view shots from the killer's perspective &amp; there's definitely a creepy chilly atmosphere to it. The film looks quite gritty &amp; is far less glossy than the average Hollywood flick which helps it as well but despite some good visuals &amp; a nice dark atmosphere I still didn't like the story &amp; that's what really sinks Black Christmas for me. The body count is low &amp; there's absolutely zero gore. Was it just me or did anyone else have problems understanding the obscene phone calls? I mean the guy speaking sounding like he was doing a bad Donald Duck impression! The ending doesn't work either on a factual level, the cops wouldn't leave Jessica alone in the house after what she had just gone through &amp; considering what had just taken place they wouldn't have left the house anyway let alone not even bother searching the attic.Technically the film is well made &amp; is pretty impressive, shot on location in Toronto, Ontario in Canada. The acting is fine, the likes of Kier Dullea, Ovlia Hussey, Margot Kidder &amp; genre favourite John Saxon put in good performances.Black Christmas is considered by some to be the very first slasher film ever made which I can see why while other's claim it's the best slasher ever made which I can't agree with at all as I think it's one of the most overrated, I'm not saying it's a bad film by any stretch of the imagination it's just one that I personally didn't like &amp; can't see why so many people do despite their reasoning. Remade by Hollywood as Black Christmas (2006) which I actually prefer as it has more of a story.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>It's the season to be sadist...fallalalla lala la la!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Considering the time it was released, this 'Black Christmas' must be regarded as slightly more important than your average slasher in which gorgeous sorority babes are being exterminated. Black Christmas is a trendsetter, opening the gates for Michael Myerses and Jason Vorheeses who'll only be popular several years later. The plot is as simple as it ever was?but here, it's new and even rather courageous! Lovely looking girls harassed by obscene phone calls and stalked by a familiar killer. Imaginatively timed around the holiday-season when the university babes are in a party mood and packing to spend Christmas with their families. Producer-director Bob Clark (who regretfully continued his career with horny adolescent crap like 'Porky's') uses many horror-clichés for the first time here: dumb cops, scream-queens, the isolated location of a fraternity house and the different stereotype-categories of female students. And ? most of all ? Black Christmas contains an old-fashioned scariness, still efficient even by today's horror standards. Finally, there still is room for comical undertones and good acting. The eminent John Saxon, but also the beautiful looking Olivia Hussey and Margot Kidder (Lois Lane!!!) Horror fans can't afford themselves to skip this one. Black Christmas is a modest milestone in the field of scary cinema.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<date>2008-03-07</date>
		<username>Michael_Elliott</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Good</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Black Christmas (1974) ** 1/2 (out of 4) Bob Clark's cult classic about a maniac terrorizing girls at a sorority house. There's no doubt this is the film that started all the 'stalk and slash' films and it's clear to see this film's influence on Halloween and while I respect this film a lot I really can't say I enjoyed all of it. There are some really great moments scattered throughout the film but at the same time I feel there are some pretty slow moments. The greatest thing is the terrific atmosphere that Clark's able to build from the terrific opening scene. I liked that fact that Clark went for atmosphere over gore and the final thirty minutes are full of suspense. The problem I have is the first hour, which is just too slow for me. I don't mind a slowly paced film but I thought everything dealing with the search of the missing girl really took away from what was important and that was the killer and the phone calls. The performances are better than average and of course there's John Saxon who's always worth watching. Again, the film has a lot of respect from me but there needed to be a few more changes to make it real good.</fullReview>
	</review>
